OK so the reshape (M, K, 2) -> (M, 2K) preserves the data. So if I load x as (M, K) row-major and then reshape, I get the same data back (just possibly interpreted differently in the mma). But this is just reshaping, not interleaving. To interleave lo and hi, I need to actually interleave the data, not just reshape. OK let me think about this more carefully. The issue is that the lo and hi data come from the SAME packed uint8 byte. I need to extract them as separate bf16 values, then interleave them with the x data. For the K-interleave in Triton, I think the best approach is: 1. Load wq as uint8 2. Compute lo and hi as bf16 3. Load x_even and x_odd as bf16 4. Interleave to get the (BLOCK_K, BLOCK_N) and (BLOCK_M, BLOCK_K) tensors For step 4, I can use a 3D reshape trick: - For w: stack lo, hi to (K/2, 2, N). Permute to (K/2, N, 2). Reshape to (K/2, 2*N). - But this concatenates along N, not K. Hmm. Actually wait, here's an idea. What if I load x in the interleaved order to begin with? x_even[m, i] = x[m, 2i] x_odd[m, i] = x[m, 2i+1] If I load x as a (M, K/2, 2) tensor where the inner dim is the even/odd, then: - x_even = x_strided[:, :, 0] - x_odd = x_strided[:, :, 1] This requires loading x with a stride pattern. In Triton, I can do this with strided loads: ```python x_even = tl.load(X_ptr + offs_m[:, None] * stride_xm + (k_start + 2 * offs_k_half)[None, :] * stride_xk) x_odd = tl.load(X_ptr + offs_m[:, None] * stride_xm + (k_start + 2 * offs_k_half + 1)[None, :] * stride_xk) ``` This is what I'm already doing. Now, for the mma, I want to compute y[m, n] = sum_k x[m, k] * w[k, n] in a single mma per K-stripe. If I can get x as (M, 2*K_half) where the rows alternate x_even and x_odd (i.e., the K-axis is interleaved), and w as (2*K_half, N) similarly interleaved, then a single mma does the trick. For w: - lo[i, n] is the weight at K = 2i (even) - hi[i, n] is the weight at K = 2i+1 (odd) - I want w_interleaved[2i, n] = lo[i, n] and w_interleaved[2i+1, n] = hi[i, n] This requires interleaving. In Triton, I can do this with a manual loop or a clever reshape. Actually, I think the cleanest way is to use a 4D approach: - lo: (K/2, 1, 1, N) -- dummy 1-dims - hi: (K/2, 1, 1, N) -- dummy 1-dims - stack: (2, K/2, 1, N) -- outer dim is lo/hi - permute: (K/2, 2, 1, N) -- second dim is lo/hi - reshape: (2*K/2, 1, N) -- Hmm Actually, let me think. The output should be (K, N) with rows [lo[0], hi[0], lo[1], hi[1], ...]. If I have a (K/2, 2, N) tensor where index (i, j, n) is the j-th element of the i-th pair, then: - index (0, 0, n) = lo[0, n] - index (0, 1, n) = hi[0, n] - index (1, 0, n) = lo[1, n] - ... - index (K/2-1, 1, n) = hi[K/2-1, n] To flatten to (K, N) with rows alternating lo and hi: - Row 0 = index (0, 0, *) = lo[0, *] - Row 1 = index (0, 1, *) = hi[0, *] - Row 2 = index (1, 0, *) = lo[1, *] - ... - Row 2i = index (i, 0, *) = lo[i, *] - Row 2i+1 = index (i, 1, *) = hi[i, *] So the row at position 2i+j is index (i, j, *). The natural flattening of (K/2, 2, N) treats (i, j) as a single dim of size 2*K/2, with the layout being: - (0, 0) -> 0 - (0, 1) -> 1 - (1, 0) -> 2 - (1, 1) -> 3 - (2, 0) -> 4 - ... So the row at position p in the flattened (2*K/2, N) tensor corresponds to (i, j) where 2i + j = p. This is the interleaved layout we want! But Triton's reshape of (K/2, 2, N) to (K, N) was giving us the N-axis interleave. So Triton's flatten of (i, j) is NOT 2i+j, it's something else. Let me re-test:

+"""Test 3D reshape (A, 2, B) -> (2A, B) to see exact layout."""
+import torch
+import triton
+import triton.language as tl
+
+@triton.jit
+def test_kernel(a_ptr, b_ptr, out_ptr, M: tl.constexpr, N: tl.constexpr):
+    i = tl.arange(0, M)
+    j = tl.arange(0, N)
+    a = tl.load(a_ptr + i[:, None] * N + j[None, :])  # (M, N) -- a[i,j] = i*N+j
+    b = tl.load(b_ptr + i[:, None] * N + j[None, :])  # (M, N) -- b[i,j] = i*N+j+100
+    j_full = tl.join(a, b)  # (M, 2, N)
+    j_reshape = tl.reshape(j_full, (M * 2, N))
+    out_offs = tl.arange(0, M * 2)[:, None] * N + tl.arange(0, N)[None, :]
+    tl.store(out_ptr + out_offs, j_reshape)
+
+
+# M=2, N=4
+# a = [[0,1,2,3], [4,5,6,7]]
+# b = [[100,101,102,103], [104,105,106,107]]
+# After join: (2, 2, 4) = [[[0,1,2,3],[100,101,102,103]], [[4,5,6,7],[104,105,106,107]]]
+# After reshape to (4, 4): which rows are which?
+# Expected if 2i+j mapping: row 0 = (0, 0, *) = a[0, *] = [0,1,2,3]
+#                            row 1 = (0, 1, *) = b[0, *] = [100,101,102,103]
+#                            row 2 = (1, 0, *) = a[1, *] = [4,5,6,7]
+#                            row 3 = (1, 1, *) = b[1, *] = [104,105,106,107]
+# Or if 2j+i mapping: row 0 = (0, 0, *) = a[0, *] = [0,1,2,3]
+#                      row 1 = (0, 1, *) = a[0, *]? No that's wrong
+# Or if (i, j) flattened with j varying fastest: row 0 = (0, 0, *) = [0,1,2,3]
+#                                                  row 1 = (0, 1, *) = [100,101,102,103]
+#                                                  row 2 = (1, 0, *) = [4,5,6,7]
+#                                                  row 3 = (1, 1, *) = [104,105,106,107]
+# OR: row 0 = (0, *, 0) = [0, 100, 4, 104]? if inner dim is "2"
+# OR: row 0 = (*, 0, 0) = [0, 100, 4, 104]? if (M, 2) is "outer" and N is "inner"
+
+a = torch.arange(8, dtype=torch.int32, device='cuda').reshape(2, 4)
+b = a + 100
+out = torch.zeros(4, 4, dtype=torch.int32, device='cuda')
+test_kernel[(1,)](a, b, out, M=2, N=4)
+print('a:')
+print(a.cpu())
+print('b:')
+print(b.cpu())
+print('Result (4, 4):')
+print(out.cpu())
